The Management Committee of the Defense Corps Holds a Citywide Corps Affairs Conference

The Management Committee of the Shanghai Defense Corps convened a corps affairs conference of the leaders of the various district corps of the city on the afternoon of the day before yesterday. The chiefs and deputy chiefs of the various district corps attended unanimously. Committee members Luo Jingyou, Yao Mulian, Wang Binyan, Wen Yingxing, Wang Yansong, and new committee member Zhang Yanrong also attended. Chairman Luo You presided over the meeting. At the beginning of the meeting, the chairman introduced the various district corps to Committee Member Zhang. Then, he gave a speech, saying that the corps affairs conference was still in its early stages. The association convened this meeting during a time when the disaster was not yet over, because of the various important relationships. The district corps should be under one system and have a unified method, and the situation in Shanghai, including the rural areas, is complex, so it is necessary to concentrate opinions at any time. Therefore, the corps affairs conference is necessary. Furthermore, after this war, the Shanghai Defense Corps suffered great losses in the war zone, and those outside the war zone were also affected. At that time, I was publicly elected to preside over the association's affairs. I originally planned to convene a meeting immediately, but I was all still recovering from the disaster and had no time to arrange things properly. Furthermore, the situation of the losses and effects had not been thoroughly investigated and reviewed, which was insufficient to clarify the situation and prepare for reorganization. Therefore, a questionnaire on the uniforms, firearms, and various items of officers and employees was made and sent to various district corps for review and submission. Then, the association sent staff to each district to verify the actual situation on the ground. At present, the verification of each corps in the non-war zone has been completed. The verification of each corps in the war zone is more difficult, and there are still two places that have not arrived. Once they are urged to attend the meeting, staff can be sent to verify them. This is one of the main reasons why the corps affairs conference was delayed. At that time, the organization of the Security Office already had a motive. The mayor was extremely interested in establishing an entire method for the Defense Corps. The association was deeply afraid that at this juncture, the planning of branches and sections would only increase the trouble of reorganization. Therefore, we conducted our own investigation and reorganization, and waited quietly for the government's orders to avoid too much change in order to be realistic. This is another reason for the delayed convocation. Now, the Security Office has been established, and the Defense Corps has been placed under its jurisdiction. The system has been determined. However, local autonomy is still in the preparatory stage, and it is feared that the organization of the corps defense will not be able to be changed for a while. The mayor attaches great importance to the Defense Corps and has also adopted false voices from various provinces and requested rules and regulations. We should actively organize to achieve perfection, which can be modeled and promoted throughout the country. This is to live up to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's earnest expectations for reorganization and to answer the elegance of the various provinces and cities' adoption and rejection. All these kinds of things have a great relationship with the corps affairs conference, so no matter how hot it is, we have to convene it immediately. You have all done a good job in managing the corps defense. I hope that you will express your great views and plan for progress together, it is said. Next, the report on the preparation of the budget for the 21st year was made, and the various district corps were asked to report in detail the location of each team and defense post. Then, the Chief Secretary Qian Zhuyu and the Chief Instructor reported on the verification situation and the points that should be paid attention to in training and storing firearms. Then, the discussion of each case began. (Case 1) How should the various district teams assist the police and how should they cooperate with the local Public Security Bureaus in each district to achieve practical cooperation? It was resolved that (1) the Defense Corps should assist as much as possible in any requests from the Public Security Bureaus in each district regarding local defense. (2) The Public Security Bureaus in each district should notify the local Defense Corps of any local security incidents in the future. (3) If the Public Security Bureau arrests a member of the corps because of a case, except for cases in which the offender is in the act or there is a special urgent situation and there is no time to notify the commander in charge, the others should be notified in advance to avoid misunderstandings. (4) The leaders of the Defense Corps in each district should contact the Public Security Bureau in each district at any time to avoid separation. The above methods, with the opinions put forward by the various district corps, were approved by the Committee Member Wen Jian and unanimously passed. (Case 2) The various district corps requested that the original funds be restored from the 21st year to maintain them. It was resolved that the funds for the Shanghai Defense Corps are extremely small. The original subsidies were already insufficient to cover the costs, and after tightening them, it became even more difficult. For several months, we have been exhausted and unable to support ourselves. Now that the Municipal Committee Office and the Fire Brigade have been restored to their original state, it is difficult for our association to be left out. We should immediately report the difficulties and request the municipal government to approve the allocation according to the new budget from the 21st year. (Case 3) How should the training methods of the various district teams be planned and carried out? It was resolved that the chief and deputy instructors will convene the instructors of the various district corps regularly to discuss together, to formulate detailed methods for unified passwords and exercises, and to review and approve the reward and punishment regulations before implementing them. (Case 4) Regarding the organization of firearms in the various district corps, (1) What is the minimum number of firearms that each team should have, and how should the deficiency be supplemented? (2) How should the methods of use and preservation be regulated? (3) How should the firearms of members of the corps who have left each district corps for various reasons be handled? It was resolved that: 1. The minimum number should be half the number of members of the corps (regardless of the type of gun). The deficiency should be raised by the local area as much as possible. If it is still insufficient, report it to the municipal government for approval. 2. The coaching stock of this association collects opinions and drafts methods of use and storage, and issues them for compliance. 3. The firearms prepared by the members of the group have been stamped and chiseled by the Defense Group, regardless of whether they are retired or not, they should be left in the group for use. If the member withdraws legally, and voluntarily donates the self-provided firearms, he should immediately report to the superior authority and give rewards, otherwise the group will give a price as appropriate. If the firearms are confiscated due to dismissal, the reasons should be stated in detail and submitted to the superiors for investigation and approval. (Case 5) Regarding the replenishment of uniforms in the various district corps and the methods for using them, it was resolved that the various district corps should first find ways to raise funds themselves, report and wait for approval. If it is still insufficient, then apply to the municipal government for funds to purchase them. The methods for using them will be drafted by the association and ordered to be followed. (Case 6) The procedures for transferring officers and the methods for admitting members of the various district corps are not consistent. How should they be regulated and organized? It was resolved that the Management Committee will formulate regulations for the appointment and removal of officers and order them to be followed. Before the promulgation, if there is any transfer of officers in the various district corps, it should be reported to the association first before approval. As for the admission and retirement of members of the corps, the original methods should be followed temporarily and handled seriously. If there are any inconsistencies with the procedures, they should be reorganized immediately. (Case 7) The official documents between this association and the various district corps should be concise, easy, and convenient. How should the format be improved? It was resolved that the format will be stipulated by the association and ordered to be followed. (Case 8) How should the troops be selected to participate in the Mayor's Double Ten Day inspection? It was resolved that the members of the corps with complete equipment should be selected by each district corps to prepare for training in advance so as to be assembled and organized and go to participate. The training methods will be discussed and decided by the coaching stock. The number of troops dispatched by each district corps on the spot is as follows: 320 people in one battalion in southern Shanghai, the accommodation arrangements in northern Shanghai are to be discussed, 180 people in one team in Yangjing, 80 people in one team in Pusong, 80 people in one team in Caojing, 80 people in one team in Fahua, and one platoon can be sent in Jiangwan if necessary, and Pengpu can be increased to two platoons. (Case 9) The loss of the teams in the war zone is huge. How should they be supplemented to restore them and benefit the local area? It was resolved that the various district corps should report the details of the losses and the minimum necessary restoration to the association, which will be forwarded to the municipal government and the war zone relief committee to request funds to be allocated for replenishment.

A Good Opportunity to Promote Domestic Goods in Southeast Asia

The Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting Domestic Goods and Tian Yi Wei Mother Company have jointly organized the Guanghua Trading Company, which is highly beneficial for promoting overseas trade of domestic goods. Yesterday, a special notice was issued to affiliated factories and members to assist in the endeavor. The notice stated:

Regarding the matter of notification, according to a letter from our member, Tian Yi Wei Mother Company, Mr. Gan Juyuan was specially dispatched last year to the Southeast Asian archipelago to promote domestic goods and foster relationships. He was honored to receive sincere welcome from overseas Chinese in various locations, who expressed enthusiastic support for domestic products, representing an excellent opportunity for expanding overseas trade. Mr. Gan's journey to Southeast Asia revealed that many Hakka people wished for our factory to establish a representative office in Shanghai to handle the export of domestic goods and the import of local products. While our factory is inherently unable to manage this concurrently, we felt compelled by circumstances to establish the Guanghua Trading Company, willing to serve the domestic goods industry. We plan to initially focus on Surabaya, Batavia, Longchuan, Makassar in the Dutch East Indies, as well as Burma and Annam. As this is a new endeavor, we are determined to succeed. Therefore, we are writing to your association, requesting you to inform all factories that if they require our services, we will serve them with utmost sincerity.

Upon receiving the letter, we have observed that overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia are enthusiastic about their motherland and deeply concerned about domestic goods. Promoting these products is bound to yield significant results. This factory possesses far-sighted vision and courageous spirit in establishing the Guanghua Trading Company to serve domestic goods factories, promote Chinese goods, and safeguard common interests. We deeply admire their dedication.

We are recording the letter and sending it to your members in the aforementioned locations. If you do not have a formal agent and wish to promote your products, please prepare samples and price lists and directly contact the company at Tian Yi General Distributor, No. 234 Zhifu Road, Shanghai (telephone number 11832), where you will find excellent and convenient solutions. We hope you will take note of this.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Issues Circular Regarding Misrepresentation of Guang Yi Factory Goods

Replies Separately to the Conscience National Salvation Corps

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce issued a circular yesterday to national civil organizations regarding the sale of cotton cloth by Yuanxiang Cotton Cloth Store under the name of Changshu Guang Yi Factory to deceive customers. It also replied separately to the Conscience National Salvation Corps regarding a certain printing and dyeing company. The original telegram and letter are as follows:

Telegram to Various Civil Organizations. For the Attention of National Civil Organizations. Our association previously received a report stating that Yuanxiang Cotton Cloth Store, located at the first house in Lane 2 of Yuyin Lane, West Shilu, Beijing Road, frequently imports large quantities of Japanese goods or affixes labels claiming genuine domestic goods or products of Changshu Guang Yi Factory in an attempt to deceive customers. After entrusting the investigation to the Cotton Cloth Trade Association, we visited the store yesterday under the pretext of brokering goods and found six single packages of fine twill and hundreds of bolts of Yuanzhi tribute cloth with the Guang Yi Factory three-star trademark. However, after investigation, it was found that there is no Guang Yi Factory in Changshu. There is only a Guang Yi Dyeing and Weaving Factory in Changzhou. Yuanxiang Store's use of Guang Yi for Guang Yi clearly indicates intentional misrepresentation and there is no doubt that they are relabeling enemy goods. We urge civil organizations in various regions to immediately intercept and investigate any products claiming to be from Guang Yi Factory with the three-star trademark to prevent confusion. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

Letter to the Conscience National Salvation Corps. For the attention of the Conscience National Salvation Corps. We have received your letter and are fully aware of its contents. You mention that certain large printing and dyeing companies and certain large dyeing and weaving factories have printing machines but no weaving machines, or that even a few factories with some weaving machines produce a quantity of goods that is disproportionate to the amount woven. However, their trademarks are all registered with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and have certificates of proof from our association and various domestic goods organizations, suggesting that they are genuine domestic goods. However, upon closer examination of their cloth, much of it is from Gongda and other factories, both domestic and foreign, which is deeply distressing. Our association is still conducting a detailed investigation into the matter of certain large printing and dyeing companies. If they purchase raw materials from other factories without using Japanese goods, it cannot be considered a violation of the agreement. Moreover, according to the domestic goods standards set by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, if the capital and management are Chinese, even if most of the raw materials are foreign, they are still recognized as fourth-class domestic goods. Therefore, various organizations have their reasons for issuing domestic goods certificates. However, if a company only dyes and does not weave, and yet claims to be a dyeing and weaving factory, it is close to deceiving the public. Therefore, our association has stopped issuing such certificates since this year. Regarding the certain large dyeing and weaving factory you mentioned, one of them was reported to be using Japanese yarn. After the matter was referred to the association, the company claimed to have temporarily suspended the weaving of this type of yarn. Another company is using Japanese cloth and is being warned by the association. We are providing this brief reply for your information. We hope you will understand.

Minutes of the Meeting of the Woolen Fabric Factory Industry Association

Thoroughly Inspect Japanese Goods

The Shanghai Chinese Woolen Fabric Factory Industry Association held a meeting of its executive committee at its meeting place on Niuzhuang Road yesterday (the 17th) at 3:00 PM. Chen Youyun, Xu Jutang, Huang Jin Yang, Huang Zhao Chang, Jiang Zongshui, and others attended. Xu Jutang chaired the meeting, and Wang Honghui served as the recorder. The following resolutions were made:

(1) To set the prices of products for each factory. First-grade camel wool cloth with stripes is priced at two liang and one qian and a half per yard, and second-grade camel wool cloth is priced at one liang and eight qian. First-grade plain camel wool cloth is priced at one liang and eight qian, and second-grade camel wool cloth is priced at one liang and six qian.

(2) To notify all factories not to purchase Japanese goods. Any factory found privately importing Japanese goods will be immediately expelled from the association and publicly announced in the newspaper to be abandoned by the public. To also notify factory residents to thoroughly inspect whether each factory is purchasing Japanese goods, and to send letters to the dyeing industry association and labor union stating that if any factories in this industry privately entrust the dyeing of Japanese yarn to their industry, they should immediately report it to this association. If they fail to report it, once discovered, the name of the dyeing shop will be publicly announced in the newspaper.

(3) All customer transactions must be in cash. If promissory notes are used, the term of the note must not be too long. If there are any unpaid bills, the industry will be notified to suspend transactions with that customer until the bills are paid, in order to demonstrate mutual assistance within the industry.

(4) To begin collecting this year's expenses from each factory starting immediately.

(5) A former broker named Ye from the Silun Factory was involved in a lawsuit with the factory. Member factories are notified to refuse to hire him.

(6) In the future, if each factory has disputes with foreign firms over orders, this association will find a way to resolve them.

Traitors Took Advantage of the Chaos to Loot During the Shanghai War

Shen Jingen Stole an Old Car

Pushed a Victim to the Ground

Took All Belongings and Escaped Without a Trace

The Police Have Apprehended the Suspect, Pending Investigation

Since the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, the Japanese army has sent large numbers of planes to bomb the war zone and the areas of Zhenru, Nanxiang, and Luodian, destroying civilian property. Zhou Shugui, who owned the Yuanda Xin Clothing Store in Luodian Town, was harassed by Japanese planes. On February 15th, at noon at around twelve o'clock, he hired car number 428, driven by local driver Shen Quangen, for a price of 15 silver dollars, to transport all the clothes from his store, packed into seven boxes with a value of more than 2,000 yuan, to Shanghai. Zhou alone accompanied the car. Unexpectedly, near the intersection of Bailinan Road and Yu Garden Road in western Shanghai, the driver, Shen Quangen, suddenly had an idea. At that time, the Sino-Japanese war was raging, and the area was desolate and uninhabited. Shen stopped the car, falsely claiming that the rear tire was broken and needed to be repaired. He asked Zhou to check the tire to see if it was damaged. Zhou did not know his plan and was about to get out of the car. Shen seized the opportunity and pushed Zhou hard, causing Zhou to fall off the car and onto the ground. Shen then drove the car at full speed and disappeared in an instant. Zhou then reported the incident to the Jing'an Temple Police Station and requested an investigation. It was not until the other day that the police station's Chinese detective Wang Yongjun and Bao detective Wu Jiwen arrested Shen Quangen (also known as Ah Er) on Edward Road and took him to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District. According to the police station's lawyer Wang Yaotang's statement of the case, the defendant is currently being prosecuted for robbery under Article 346 of the Criminal Law, but this may need to be amended in the future. The police station's investigation revealed that the defendant was not a car driver. The car was stolen from Edward Road in January. On February 3, he stole a license plate number 4286 from Minti Niyin Road in the French Concession, removed the number 6, and hung it on the stolen car, making it number 428. He specialized in soliciting business everywhere. On February 15, the defendant took Zhou's business in Luodian and pushed Zhou off the car in the middle of the road and drove away. Now, because all the stolen goods have not been investigated, the lawyer requested an extension. According to Zhou Shugui's complaint of the above situation and the statement that it was indeed the defendant who drove the car and pushed him off, when questioned, the defendant denied it, saying that he was farming in the countryside that day and could be investigated. After the judge, Ge Shixun, reviewed the confession, he ordered the defendant to be detained for seven days for further investigation.

The Social Affairs Bureau Schedules Factory Inspections

Announces Initial Scope of Inspection

After the promulgation and implementation of the Factory Law and the Factory Inspection Law, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has set up a special section and appointed qualified factory inspectors to conduct inspections according to the law. Just as everything was about to be completed, the January 28th Incident occurred, causing it to be suspended without implementation. Now that the ceasefire agreement has been signed and order has been restored, the bureau has actively prepared and scheduled to begin the initial inspections on September 1. The details are as follows:

Scope of Inspection. The bureau issued a notice to all factories yesterday instructing them on the initial scope of inspection. The original order is as follows: "For compliance, this bureau has scheduled to implement the initial inspection in accordance with the provisions of the Factory Inspection Law starting on September 1. The scope is as follows: (1) Factory books. Factories should prepare a register of workers, a report form for worker injuries and illnesses, a report form for disaster events, and a report form for retired workers, and submit them to this bureau on a regular basis in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the Factory Law. (2) Working hours. Worker working hours should be handled in accordance with the provisions of Articles 8 to 12 of the Factory Law. Any extension of working hours should be reported to this bureau with detailed reasons in accordance with the provisions of Article 6 of the Implementation Regulations of the Factory Law. (3) Wages. The determination of worker wage rates and the payment of wages should be handled in accordance with the provisions of Articles 20 to 25 of the Factory Law. (4) Bonuses or profit sharing. In accordance with the provisions of Article 40 of the Factory Law, workers should receive bonuses or profit sharing, and methods should be formulated and reported to this bureau in accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the Implementation Regulations of the Factory Law. (5) Worker allowances and compensation. Allowances and compensation for workers who are injured or die as a result of performing their duties should be handled in accordance with the provisions of Articles 45 and 46 of the Factory Law and Articles 29 to 31 of the Implementation Regulations of the Factory Law. (6) Apprentices. Factories that employ apprentices should be handled in accordance with the provisions of Articles 56 to 67 of the Factory Law. If there are difficulties in submitting apprenticeship contracts, the contents of the contract may be extracted and submitted to the bureau for verification. (7) Factory regulations. The formulation or modification of factory regulations should be reported to this bureau in accordance with the provisions of Article 75 of the Factory Law. In addition to separate orders, this order is issued for compliance."

Inspection Methods. The bureau will send personnel to inspect each factory. The name of the inspector and the date of inspection must be notified to the factory one week in advance. At the appointed time, the inspector will bring the forms and fill them out while inquiring and consulting the books from the factory. If necessary, workers may be summoned for questioning to obtain evidence. The factory shall fill out and report matters that should be reported in accordance with the law within a deadline determined by the inspector, and the person in charge of the factory shall sign and seal the inspection form to show solemnity. The aforementioned deadline shall not exceed the end of this year. If a factory is unable to report within the deadline set by the inspector due to special circumstances, it shall report the reasons in detail and apply for an extension. Failure to report after the deadline will be punished in accordance with the law. Inspections are usually conducted during the day, but if there are factories with night work, the inspector may also go at night if necessary.

Inspection Areas. The bureau's initial inspections are carried out in phases by area, rotating through Hunan, Longhua, Zhabei, Pusong, Jiangwan, Wusong, Pudong, and the two special districts of the Public Concession and the French Concession. On average, each inspector will inspect one factory per day.

The Citizens' Association Sent a Letter to the Municipal Party Department Yesterday, Painstakingly Explaining the Pros and Cons of Reducing and Exempting Rent

The Shanghai Citizens' Association sent a letter to the Shanghai Special City Party Department yesterday regarding the reduction and exemption of rent, expressing its views sincerely and pertinently. The original text is as follows:

"Respectfully presented, we have investigated that the reduction and exemption of rent in Shanghai is indeed an important plan for seeking the welfare of the masses, and it is also a long-term consideration for landlords. The situation of the city cannot be thoroughly relieved. Today's situation is a temporary relief, but tomorrow it will be a major disaster. If the department has taken this into consideration, please ask the central government to send personnel to supplement the shortfall. This is to seek the welfare of the masses. However, the landlords who are short-sighted will definitely use the municipal government's rent exemption method, regardless of the suffering of the masses, and carry out their bone-sucking behavior. They will sue in court, and the court will ignore the facts of social economy and not know the basic principle of law, "the welfare of the masses is the highest law," (Latin: Salus Populi Est Suprema Lex; English: The Welfare of the People is the Supreme Law) and dare not cite the provisions of the Civil Code on rent reduction and exemption. As a result, the commercial city will inevitably decline and perish. To that point, the landlords and tenants will perish together, and the original plan will not be reduced. In addition to the municipal government, the court will not escape its responsibility. When encountering rent reduction and exemption cases, the civil code's rent reduction and exemption provisions should be invoked in accordance with the law, so that the city can restore its vitality and the landlords and tenants can obtain their permanent welfare. This is a public convenience. This is presented to the Shanghai Special City Party Department of the Chinese Kuomintang."

The Fisheries Administration Bureau Will Establish a Shellfish Aquaculture Experimentation Field

▲ Site Located in Zhenhai Bay Pond

The Marine Fisheries Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang regions, formerly based in this city, had all of its undertakings seemingly halted due to government austerity measures. However, various plans were still underway. Recently, they proposed establishing a shellfish aquaculture experimentation field in the Zhenhai Bay Pond. This plan has been completed and submitted to the Ministry of Industry for instructions a few days ago. Approval for commencement is expected soon. The bureau's official submission and plan are recorded below:

▲ Official Submission: Requesting Approval and Implementation of Shellfish Aquaculture Experimentation Plan and Budget

To comply with the order to report on the planned shellfish aquaculture experimentation, a detailed plan and budget have been prepared. We respectfully request your review and implementation. Your ministry's directive states: "Having noted your submission, the Haizhou Aquatic Product Experimentation Field is currently being prepared for restoration by the ministry. Your request to transfer it to your bureau for management is not approved. However, to improve fisheries, your bureau may first establish a shellfish aquaculture experimentation field on the originally acquired Zhenhai tidal flats. Within the scope of your bureau's organizational regulations, prepare a detailed plan and separate budget for review and approval." Respectfully, regarding the preparation of shellfish aquaculture experimentation, previous submissions have been made to your ministry, and instructions have been received and followed. At this time of strict government austerity, to comply with the order to tighten spending, we propose to temporarily designate an area of 1,000 mu within the acquired public tidal flats to initially engage in the aquaculture of razor clams and blood clams. If there are no special changes, the income should be considerable. After detailed planning, the required expenses have been reduced to 61,830 yuan, while the estimated income is approximately 84,000 yuan. This budget has been repeatedly reviewed and is truly reduced to the bare minimum. Due to the preceding order, we respectfully submit the Shellfish Aquaculture Experimentation Field Plan and Shellfish Aquaculture Experimentation Field Budget for your review and implementation. This would be greatly beneficial.

▲ Shellfish Aquaculture Experimentation Field Plan: (1) Organization: To save on expenses, the organization of the Shellfish Aquaculture Experimentation Field established by this bureau will be kept simple. It will consist of only one Field Director/Chief, two technicians, and twenty-one aquaculture workers, all stationed at the field to handle various affairs. (2) Site: The site of this field is located in Zhenhai Bay Pond. According to records, 7,071 mu, 7 fen, 8 li, and 4 hao of tidal flats were allocated from the old Ningbo Shatian Sub-bureau of Zhejiang last year. The soil quality is excellent, and the bait is abundant, making it very suitable for shellfish aquaculture. (3) Aquaculture Species: The aquaculture species in this field will initially be razor clams and blood clams. Other shellfish will be aquacultured when sufficient funds are available. (4) Area: The area of this field is temporarily set at 1,000 mu, with 800 mu for razor clams and 200 mu for blood clams. (5) Budget: All expenses for this field are based on a tight budget, with estimated temporary expenses of 12,350 yuan and annual recurring expenses of 49,480 yuan. The recurring budget and annual income budget are listed below: (Recurring Expenditure) Salaries: 8,400 yuan, Office Expenses: 960 yuan, Special Expenses: 39,640 yuan, Razor Clam Seedlings: 30,400 yuan, Blood Clam Seedlings: 9,000 silver dollars, Travel Expenses: 240 yuan, Contingency Fund: 480 yuan, (Temporary Expenses) Land Cost: 600 taels, Construction Cost: 3,900 yuan, Procurement Cost: 3,850 yuan, Preparation Cost: 4,000 yuan, (Recurring Income) Razor Clam Income: 7,200 yuan (800 mu, after one and a half years of aquaculture, each mu can yield about 4.5 dan of blood clams, with each dan worth about 100 yuan, totaling the above amount.), Blood Clam Income: 3,000 yuan (200 mu, after one and a half years of aquaculture, each mu can yield about 3 dan of blood clams, with each dan worth about 30 yuan, totaling the above amount.)

Public Bus Company Strike Trend Becomes More Serious

▲ Workers Hold a General Meeting to Discuss Solutions

▲ The Strike Committee Sends a Letter to the Ratepayers' Association Seeking Assistance

Since the public bus workers declared a strike, the situation has become increasingly serious due to the intransigent attitude of the company's Superintendent, Short. Details of yesterday's events are recorded below:

▲ Workers' General Meeting: Due to the company's tough stance and disregard for the workers' livelihoods, all workers, numbering over 200, convened a general meeting at the Renhe Teahouse on Wuding Road at 2 PM yesterday. The presidium reported on the negotiations with the drivers and resolved to request mediation from party and government authorities and to send a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association for assistance to avoid a major dispute.

▲ Letter to the Ratepayers' Association: The Public Bus Strike Committee sent a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concession, stating: "Respected Sirs, on July 25th, the company's managers, Short, Trittly, and Pear, summoned worker representatives Wang Xingmao, Shi Baoshan, and four others to the transport office for discussions. Short initially proposed improving practices due to the company's stagnant revenue, requesting that all workers refrain from malpractice. The company would increase each worker's salary by 5/10, totaling 37.5 yuan per month, up from the original 23.5 yuan. The worker representatives reported back to all workers, who were satisfied and willing to continue working. However, after Manager Trittly went to Japan on a two-week leave, entrusting all matters to Pear, Pear dismissed over 20 workers without cause after only one week in charge, shocking all workers. The original six representatives were sent to negotiate and demand the implementation of the promised salary increase, but Pear not only refused the workers' demands but also intensified the oppression, leading to an unbearable spontaneous strike. Representatives were then sent to demand that the company accept the conditions, but they were repeatedly rejected. The company now disregards the workers' suffering and is recruiting new workers, leaving the original workers with no means of support. We have nowhere to turn. Knowing that you are dedicated to protecting the interests of the Chinese and devoted to public service, we have specially dispatched Wang Xingmao, Shi Baoshan, and others as full representatives to meet with you. We humbly request your audience and ask that you have compassion for the suffering of over 300 workers, agreeing to mediate to maintain their livelihoods and demanding that the company stop recruiting new workers to avoid a major dispute that could disrupt local security."

▲ Strike Committee Statement: According to Strike Committee member number 150, a statement was released to the Dagongshe reporter yesterday: "I am shocked to learn that some newspapers have referred to me as a 'running dog' and accused me of asking workers to stop beating White Russians and blocking buses. I have always represented the workers' interests since being elected as their representative. Moreover, six representatives went to negotiate with the company, and all negotiation details have been announced to the workers. There is no possibility of a third party undermining and dividing the workers' solidarity. In the future, we will continue to fight within legal boundaries and will not be discouraged by sabotage."

▲ Drivers Offer Support: After all ticket sellers declared a strike, they had considerable negotiations with the drivers beforehand. During yesterday's general meeting, the drivers also sent representatives to attend, expressing strong dissatisfaction with the company's oppression of workers. They resolved to stand with the workers and actively offer support. If the issue cannot be resolved within two or three days, all drivers will join in the support, potentially expanding the strike.

▲ Another Warning: The Strike Committee stated that Factory Director and Superintendent Short posted a notice at the company entrance on Kangnai Road yesterday, recruiting new workers. Over 100 people have already applied. The Strike Committee believes that this strike was caused by the company's unwarranted oppression and unbearable suffering. The recruitment of new workers while the strike remains unresolved will affect the strike's prospects. They issued another warning to the new workers yesterday, advising them not to take the job; otherwise, they would be considered to have violated strike discipline and would be dealt with forcefully. As a result, striking workers forcibly removed the uniforms of over a dozen new ticket sellers on Kangnai Road yesterday.

▲ Throwing Excrement: The Xin Sheng She reported that the company continued to attempt to run buses on routes 1, 2, 5, 6, and 9 yesterday to facilitate transportation. Passengers were few, fearing being caught in the crossfire of the striking workers. At 12 PM, as a route 9 bus traveled near the Great World amusement park, striking workers scooped out watermelons, filled them with excrement, and threw them into the bus. The stench filled the air, and the passengers were forced to endure the foul odor. A similar incident occurred at Jing'an Temple at 12 PM in the afternoon.

Recent Situation of the Catastrophic Disaster in Wugong, Shaanxi Province

This year, Wugong County, Shaanxi Province, suffered black frost in March, accompanied by howling winds and hail. Although there was a single rainfall afterward, the young crops had withered, and drought conditions had formed. People were tearing down houses for firewood and fleeing from famine with their families, enduring extreme hardship and suffering that was unbearable to witness. Furthermore, since the start of summer, the epidemic has worsened daily, resulting in countless deaths. Desolate cries fill the land, awaiting burial in ditches and gullies. The tragic disaster situation has been reported in newspapers. Now, as autumn arrives without rain, the drought and pestilence worsen daily, leaving the people with no escape from death. The Shanghai Chinese Relief Society has received numerous reports from the Shaanxi Relief Society branch and gentry of Wugong County, requesting relief assistance. The society, unable to save due to a lack of funds but unwilling to ignore the situation, reluctantly raised 8,500 yuan for urgent relief and 1,500 yuan from the Xinwei Relief Society, totaling 10,000 yuan. They publicly appointed Mr. Wang Jishi, a gentry member of Wugong County and director of the Wugong Orphanage Training Center, as the director. They also sent a letter to Mr. Lu Hefu, chairman of the Chang'an Relief Society branch in Shaanxi, asking him to select members to assist. Relief efforts have already begun. The society has sent letters requesting detailed reports on the relief efforts and the situation of the disaster victims. Furthermore, due to the current widespread epidemic and the scarcity of effective medicines, the society has distributed 3,600 bottles of Jisheng Dan (relief pills) to the Shaanxi Relief Society, 3,000 bottles of Jisheng Dan to Mr. Wang Jishi in Wugong, and 16,900 bottles of Jisheng Dan in five shipments to Mr. Lu Hefu of the Chang'an branch in Shaanxi. They have also sent 500 bottles of Feilong Duoming Dan (Flying Dragon Life-Saving Pills) and 500 bottles of Lingbao Miaoying Dan (Lingbao Miraculous Response Pills) in succession to provide relief and protect the lives of the people, hoping to avert the disaster.

Based on the above situation, the cholera epidemic this year has decreased. It is hoped that it will gradually disappear in the Shanghai area in the coming weeks. (2) During this long period of hot and humid weather, there was a major thunderstorm on the evening of Thursday, August 11th, covering almost the entire city of Shanghai. The same wind and rain occurred again the following night, but afterward, the temperature and humidity increased. (3) The areas most affected by this year's cholera epidemic are Henan and Shaanxi. In Luoyang alone, it is reported that there were 50,000 cases and 10,000 deaths. In 12 counties in Shaanxi, there were 22,000 deaths. In the provincial capital of Xi'an, nearly 100 people are dying daily from the epidemic. The epidemic is also very severe in Shandong, Shaanxi, Gansu, and Hubei provinces, and even remote villages and towns are affected. According to a report from Hankou at the end of last week (August 6th), there were 156 cholera cases, with 24 deaths. (4) Fortunately, reports recently received from several epidemic areas indicate that the epidemic is gradually subsiding, similar to Shanghai. In Nanjing, only 120 cholera cases were reported in the week ending August 13th, with 48 deaths. There were only 11 cases in Guangzhou, with no deaths. There were only 6 cases in Tianjin, also with no deaths. There were only 2 deaths in Wuchang and Suiyuan. (5) This office has declared the following seaports within its jurisdiction as cholera-infected ports: (A) Dalian and Niuzhuang were declared infected ports on August 10th. (B) Yantai was declared an infected port on August 14th. (6) According to records from the South Manchuria Railway Health Department, 1,729 cholera cases were discovered from June to August 8th. Of these, Dalian accounted for 1,366 cases, Yingkou within the railway area accounted for 55 cases, Liaoyang 10 cases, Mukden 12 cases, and Changchun 75 cases. The epidemic is also very severe in Fushun, and several hundred cases have been discovered in Harbin. (7) This office is currently producing a 1,200-foot-long cholera film that clearly explains the causes, prevention, and treatment of cholera. It also features various scenery, people, and health organizations in Shanghai and its surrounding areas, such as hospitals and laboratories. It will soon be shown in various well-known cinemas and to the public. It is expected to arouse the audience's interest, no less than the "Yan History of the Imperial Palace."

The Death of Female Workers After a Japanese Ship Capsized Their Boat - Family Members Appeal

▲ Petitioning the Municipal Government to Negotiate Compensation with the Japanese Side

On the afternoon of August 9th, around 6 PM, a boat carrying 14 female workers from Qichang Pier in Pudong capsized while crossing the Huangpu River to work at factories in Puxi. The boat was suddenly hit by the Japanese ship Hakone Maru, which was turning around. The waves capsized the boat, causing all the female workers to fall into the river. With the exception of Qu Huoying, who was rescued, the remaining 13 drowned. Their bodies were subsequently recovered, identified by their families, and prepared for burial. According to previous reports, there were 13 deaths in total (previous reports of 11 were incorrect). The families of the deceased, Wu Yang, mother of Wu Pindi, Lu Zhenxiu, sister of Lu Xiangdi, Chen Kang, mother of Chen Jinxiu, Li Wang, mother of Li Amu, Gong Jinguai, father of Gong Xiaomei, Gong Zhulin, father of Gong Linbao, Huang Xushi, aunt of Huang Meiqian, Yang Fanshi, mother of Yang Jincui, Shi Xushi, sister-in-law of Shi Yangxiaoyuan, Lu Xiaoshi, aunt of Lu Gu Jinbao, Huang Lishi, sister of Huang Xiaoling, Ni Zhangshi, mother of Ni Lingdi, and Yuan Shanlai, father of Yuan Awen, totaling 13 families, stated that according to shipping regulations, there must be two officers stationed on the deck of a ship. The Hakone Maru's officers saw the boat behind the ship being hit by the waves, but they did not order the driver to stop the engine, causing the tragedy. The blame is undeniable. Furthermore, the families are poor, and they no longer have the income from the workers' wages. Now, with the loss of their loved ones, they are in deep grief. Yesterday, they jointly submitted a petition to the Municipal Government, stating the reasons and requesting that the government negotiate with the Japanese Consul General in Shanghai, demanding that the Toyo Company, owner of the Hakone Maru, provide compensation to value human life. At the same time, they appealed to philanthropists to provide relief to maintain their livelihoods.

Conclusion of the Trial of Fan Hongsheng for the Murder of Wang Wenying

▲ Sentencing on the 24th

Fan Hongsheng (aka Fan Ruikun) from Nanjing is under serious suspicion for the murder of female physiognomist Wang Wenying. He was detained by the police and brought before the First Special Court. Fan's lawyer, Jiang Baoyi, presented various pieces of evidence to prove that Fan had a mental illness. The details of the trial have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide of the Criminal Court held a continuation of the trial. First, he questioned Wang Wenying's maid, Chen Ajin, briefly. Then he questioned Fan Hongsheng, who suddenly completely overturned his confessions in the police station and his testimony at the first trial, denying that he had killed Wang Wenying. He claimed that his initial confessions were not voluntary. The court then summoned the Chinese detective in charge of the case, Su Changsheng, to ask if Fan's confessions in the police station were voluntary. Su replied that they were entirely voluntary and that there was no coercion. Judge Feng then ordered the start of the closing arguments. First, the police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that based on the testimony of the deceased's mother, Wang Wushi, and others, it could be inferred that the reason for Fan's murder was that he had been rejected in his attempt to propose marriage to Wang Wenying. The defendant presented witnesses and physical evidence to demonstrate the defendant's various states of mental illness, such as sitting on top of a car, using flies as food, and dancing with Indian police officers on the road. However, these are not sufficient to prove that he was also mentally incompetent at the time of the crime. The defendant bought cigarettes from the maid Chen Ajin with two pieces of lead money to avoid suspicion, fled the scene after the fact, and discarded the bloody clothes used in the murder. These are all sufficient to prove that the defendant was unusually clear-headed and no different from ordinary people at the time of the crime. Therefore, he should be sentenced to death according to law. However, because the defendant had a mental breakdown when he divorced his wife, Yang Xiuying, his mental capacity may be weaker than that of ordinary people. Therefore, he requested a slight reduction in the sentence to life imprisonment. The defendant's lawyer, Jiang Baoyi, replied that the diagnosis of mental illness is very difficult. Because the disease sometimes appears to be no different from ordinary people, even doctors cannot make a judgment and it must be assessed by an expert. In the past, someone was diagnosed with a mental illness only after more than a year of assessment by an expert. This shows how difficult diagnosis is. It is wrong to arbitrarily conclude that he does not have the disease simply because the defendant was not found to be mentally incompetent before and after his arrest. He also cited the writings of British and American mental health experts as evidence and asked the court to declare the defendant not guilty in accordance with Article 31 of the Criminal Law, which stipulates that acts committed by those who are mentally incapacitated are not punishable. The plaintiff Wang Wushi's lawyer, Dong Qin, filed an attached civil suit, demanding compensation of 12,000 yuan, calculated at 400 yuan per year for 30 years. However, Wang Wushi herself stated that she only wanted Fan Hongsheng to pay with his life and that Cheng Meixian should pay the 12,000 yuan. Judge Feng then declared the closing arguments concluded and scheduled sentencing for the 24th.

Ye Lishao Accuses Xu Jiping of Abducting Their Child

▲Xu Claims Illness and Fails to Appear

▲Jurisdiction Still Under Investigation

Hu Bingheng, the manager of Jin Cheng Qian Zhuang, had an affair with Xu Jiping (also known as Xu Zhongyi), a female student from Chih Tze University, and they rented a house to live together, seemingly as husband and wife. However, the woman had long been betrothed by her parents to Ye Lishao of Fengjing as his wife. Ye was initially unaware of Xu's activities in Shanghai, so he still married her according to custom. Xu then found herself in a situation where she was involved with two men simultaneously, which lasted for five or six years. Until last year, Xu finally requested a divorce from Ye, inviting Ye to Shanghai. They drew up a divorce agreement at the Da Zhonghua Hotel on Xizang Road, stipulating that their son, Duansheng, would remain Ye's child but would be raised by Xu until he turned sixteen, at which point he would be returned to Ye. The necessary education and upbringing expenses would be paid by Ye. Both parties signed the agreement and hired lawyer Yang Changchi to witness it, ensuring its validity. From then on, Xu believed that she could live happily ever after with Hu Bingheng. However, she later felt that Hu was not genuinely in love with her and became deeply suspicious of his previous claim that his first wife had passed away, wondering if it was not true. Therefore, she demanded a written guarantee to put her mind at ease. Hu then wrote a document stating that if he were found to still have a wife, he would pay her 100,000 yuan as compensation. Unexpectedly, before the ink was even dry, Xu discovered that Hu had a legal wife. She negotiated with him, but without satisfactory results. Consequently, she initially filed a criminal complaint against Hu for abandonment with the First Special District Court and then a civil lawsuit against Hu for breach of contract, demanding a judgment ordering him to pay the 100,000 yuan compensation and confirming her marital status with Hu. When the civil court opened the trial, Hu invited Xu's ex-husband, Ye Lishao, to testify. Ye then accused Xu of abducting his son, Duansheng, intending to use the child to extort money from others. Yesterday afternoon, the trial for Ye's case against Xu was scheduled to begin. At 2:30 PM, Judge Fu Lin ascended to the fifth courtroom. However, the defendant, Xu Jiping, claimed illness and did not appear. According to her lawyer, there was a jurisdictional issue in this case that should be investigated first. Since Xu resided in the French Concession and cohabitated with Hu in Yuanchang Lane on Julong Road, and then moved to No. 88 Huayuan Lane when the lawsuit with Hu began, none of these locations fell under the jurisdiction of the court. The plaintiff's lawyer then stated that the financial fraud element of the plaintiff's accusation was based on the divorce agreement, which was negotiated at the Da Zhonghua Hotel on Xizang Road and signed at the law office of Yang Changchi. Therefore, the location of the crime fell within the court's jurisdiction and should be accepted by the court. Judge Fu felt that this point required further investigation and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Prison Guard in Women's Prison Illegally Delivers Opium to Inmate

A woman named Du Wenshi was recently arrested and sentenced for opium use and imprisoned in the women's prison of the First Special District Court. At 5:30 AM on the 13th of this month, a person named Ye paid 10 yuan to bribe Mai Wen, a Cantonese prison guard at the women's prison gate, to deliver a small packet of opium to the female guard leader, Guo Huijun, instructing her to pass it on to the female inmate, Du Wenshi. Guo immediately reported the incident, along with the opium, to the warden, Huang Yaohua, who detained Mai. The prosecutor, Zhong Qingzhi, concluded the preliminary investigation on the previous day, confirming that Mai had committed a criminal act. The prosecutor then notified the Shanghai Municipal Council's Legal Department to prosecute him according to the law. Mai was handed over to the police of the Municipal Council for detention and was escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the Special Court yesterday morning. According to the police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, the defendant was being prosecuted under Article 29, Section 12 of the Criminal Law for dereliction of duty and Article 13 of the Anti-Opium Law. Subsequently, the female guard Guo Huijun testified that the defendant had handed her a small paper packet that morning, asking her to pass it on to the female inmate Du Wenshi, saying that it contained opium and promising to reward her with five yuan. She refused and warned him not to violate the law, urging him to leave immediately. However, the defendant persisted, so she reported the incident, along with the packet, to the warden. The warden opened the packet and found four white pills and two opium pellets. He then summoned Mai for questioning and reported the matter to the prosecutor's office for investigation. When questioned, the defendant claimed that Guo had asked him to buy aspirin for a headache on the 12th for one yuan, which he then delivered to her the next morning at a paper shop next to the court. He denied delivering opium. He said that there was another reason for the accusation. After the former warden, Madam Fang, was dismissed, Guo and others suspected that he and others had spoken against her, so they were now framing him and requested an investigation. Judge Ge ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing for seven days later to investigate the matter further.

Wu Jianguang's Son's Scandal Resolved

Wu Zhongliang, the son of Wu Jianguang, had previously engaged in a physical relationship with Shen Ai'e, a female employee of the ABC Commercial Press on Jiujiang Road. However, he recently abandoned her, prompting Shen's mother, Shen Chushi, to hire lawyer Xue Jiaqi to sue Wu for enticement in the First Special Court. Wu Zhongliang also hired Zheng Wenkai as his lawyer to defend him and file a counterclaim. All details of the trial have been reported in this newspaper. The lawyers of both parties have now mediated a settlement, and the settlement has been established. The settlement agreement is transcribed below: Settlement Agreement Attached to Civil Lawsuit: Shen Chushi and Wu Zhongliang, after mediation by both parties' lawyers, both parties are willing to settle the dispute. Wu Zhongliang will pay Shen Chushi 600 yuan, and the mediator will add 100 yuan, totaling 700 yuan, to be paid in full on the date of signing. Shen Chushi is willing to immediately withdraw the private prosecution, and Wu Zhongliang will also immediately withdraw the counterclaim. Neither party will pursue any further disputes.

Gengxin Theater Destroyed

▲Entire Building Consumed by Fire

▲Estimated Loss of Approximately 30,000 to 40,000

The Lin Ji Gengxin Theater at the intersection of Menggu Road in Zhabei ceased operations after the Shanghai Incident. After the Shanghai Armistice Agreement was reached and the Japanese troops withdrew, it was taken over by Gu and others. Starting in early June, they extensively renovated the interior, repainted everything, and added more than 500 new chairs. The renovation had been completed and they planned to reopen before the traditional Mid-Autumn Festival. Yesterday morning at 3:35 AM, the theater's watchmen, Wang Yongshan (age 57, from Hebei), Guo Yuqing (age 32, from Tianjin), and Li Yuanlin, were sleeping downstairs near the staircase because of the heat. Zhang, a tutor from one of the shareholders' families, along with a Mr. Chen and a tailor Mr. Jia, were sleeping upstairs in the accounting room. Unexpectedly, just as they were sound asleep, a crackling sound was heard from the west side of the ticket office downstairs. Watchman Guo Yuqing immediately woke up and saw smoke billowing and flames spreading rapidly. He shouted loudly, and the sleepers jumped up to get water to extinguish the fire. However, the walls were freshly painted and easily flammable, so the fire spread rapidly and became uncontrollable. The fire brigades from the nearby sections arrived in their fire trucks and bravely fought the fire until about 7 AM, when it was finally extinguished. The interior tables, chairs, and stage were completely destroyed. It was reported that some of the scenery and costumes were also reduced to ashes. The theater had been hastily prepared and was not insured, so the estimated loss was between 30,000 and 40,000 yuan. It was also reported that when the fire was raging, Zhang and Chen, who were sleeping upstairs, were eager to escape and jumped out of the window, sustaining serious injuries from the fall. The cause of the fire is still unclear. The police from the First Branch of the Fourth District detained the watchmen Wang Yongshan and Guo Yuqing for questioning.

Huadong Factory Donates Festival Funds to Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteers

Chen Youyun and Qiu Xinyi, the managers of the Huadong Woolen and Camel Hair Factory, and all of its employees, felt moved by the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteers' efforts to resist the invaders and protect the country. They specially donated 30 yuan from the factory's Mid-Autumn Festival feast to the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteers. This practice of donating festival funds to support the troops should be emulated by all businesses in Shanghai to save the Northeast from its plight.

Shihua Bookstore Pioneering Sales to Support Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteers

▲Purchase a Copy of "The Biography of General Ma Zhanshan"

▲Long-Term Donation of 10 Cents to the Volunteer Army from Each Sale

At a time when the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteers are engaged in a bloody battle with the enemy and urgently need funds, while various sectors have made many donations, those who can provide long-term support are still rare. It was recently learned that Shihua Bookstore on Danfeng Road, inside Xiaodongmen, recognizing this need, has specially decided to donate 10 cents to the Volunteer Army from the sale price of each newly published copy of "The Biography of General Ma Zhanshan," setting a precedent for all industries. The bookstore also plans to publish the names of the book buyers to promote this righteous cause. It is reported that the book was written by Mr. Zhang Nannong and begins with the General's family history, starting with his grandfather and great-grandfather. It then describes the chivalrous marriage of his parents in their youth, the deeds of the General in his youth and adulthood, various anecdotes about his wife and mother, and the behind-the-scenes details of his recent daring capture of the enemy in their den to resist the Japanese and oppose the traitors. These details are generally unknown to the outside world and are not comparable to novels that are simply compiled from newspaper clippings and fabricated stories. The General's representative, Mr. Han Liru, has personally signed the book, confirming that the recorded events are true. The book also includes prefaces from prominent figures from all sectors of society, amounting to over a hundred, all reproduced as zinc plates and printed on high-quality paper, making it valuable. The entire book consists of two thick volumes and sells for only 1.20 yuan, with a long-term donation of 10 cents to the Volunteer Army, making it easy and accessible for people to contribute and accumulate small amounts into a significant sum. The actions of the bookstore are truly commendable.

Jiaotong Travel Agency Declaration

The Jiaotong Travel Agency was initiated and established by prominent figures in Shanghai, including Wang Xiaolai, Wang Binyan, Gao Guanwu, Feng Zhihe, Li Guangzhen, and Ke Juchu. The preparatory office is located at No. 35 Renji Road on Sichuan Road. Yesterday, the initiators of the agency issued a declaration to all sectors, the original text of which is as follows: "Declaration" Dr. Sun Yat-sen said, "Clothing, food, housing, and transportation are the four major needs of human life." As for transportation, although our country has many trains and waterways, making travel convenient, the protection of merchants and travelers lacks adequate mechanisms. In major commercial ports across the country, upon the arrival of trains and ships, one can see porters swarming and rushing, bumping and jostling, surrounding and obstructing, clamoring and extorting, which is far from orderly and resembles banditry. This situation directly reflects the weaknesses of the country and society, increasing the lament of travelers and merchants, who often lose items and have their goods stolen. This chaotic state is enough to show the weakness of the nation and the chaos of society, increasing the sighs of merchants and travellers, and everyone who has been on a journey has experienced this. Therefore, to ensure the safety of travelers, planning and construction are essential. One can observe the tranquility of train arrivals and the orderliness of traffic in Western countries, where civilization and transportation are increasingly convenient. Although there are those in our country who care about social construction and know that travel agencies are indispensable in modern times, even if established, their convenience cannot be extended to ordinary people. Recognizing this, we embrace high aspirations to seek national glory, social order, travel safety, and human happiness. Through extensive research, we have gathered the resources and intelligence of many individuals to contribute to society. Therefore, we plan to organize the Jiaotong Travel Agency, providing affordable cargo transportation, proper reception and sending-off services, and striving to make convenience accessible to ordinary people, so that they can truly feel at home. The preparatory period has already lasted for two months. The standard capital is set at 100,000 yuan, operating as a limited liability company. However, our knowledge is limited, and our resources are insufficient. We hope that prominent figures in society will not hesitate to offer advice and guidance, so that the Jiaotong Travel Agency can be perfected and realized as soon as possible. This would be fortunate for us and fortunate for society. We hereby declare.

Elderly Accountant Commits Suicide Due to Unemployment

Sun Axiang (age 30), a Ningbo native who previously worked as a senior accountant at Kongshi Foreign Firm, had recently been unemployed and was residing at the dental clinic of Song Kangqi at No. 334, Six Malu, with his sister, Fu Sunshi, who provided him with food and clothing. Although Sun repeatedly asked people to help him find a job, he was consistently disappointed. As a result, he developed a pessimistic outlook on life and secretly ingested opium to commit suicide. After being discovered, he was sent to Renji Hospital. However, due to severe poisoning, he soon died. The hospital notified the Laozha Gate Police Station, which dispatched detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the morgue for examination. Yesterday morning, Zhan Liangce, the prosecutor delegated by the First Special District Court, arrived at the morgue to conduct the examination. He opened the case and heard the testimony of Song Kangqi, who stated that the deceased's sister had been renting a room from him for four or five years and that he had always seen the siblings getting along well. On the day in question, he found the deceased sleeping in bed, looking pale and foaming at the mouth, so he sent him to the hospital for treatment. Fu Sunshi, his sister, also provided a statement. After reviewing the testimonies, Prosecutor Zhan concluded that Sun Axiang had died from opium poisoning before death, and the body was handed over to his sister for funeral arrangements.
