Free Talk

Second First Branch Discussion

Stringing Up a Flying Eagle

— Zhan Lu

An eagle is a bird of prey!

The iron bird in the sky is even fiercer than your flying eagle! Not knowing to grieve for the rabbit when it dies, or to commiserate with its own kind! Yet it used its own iron bird to harm its own flying eagle! Pitiful eagle! Sinking, oh so sinking, sinking, oh so sinking, the flying eagle has turned into a hidden scale! Ate your eagle meat, returned your eagle bones, that can be considered a show of humanity! What is humanity? It is being prepared to string up flying eagles. I have just casually composed this limerick, and I also have to explain the matter of this poem... The Guangdong province, because of the naval incident, sunk the Republic of China's aircraft and bombarded the Republic of China's destroyer, which everyone thought was a pity! According to Guangdong's side, the authorities thought that the ship was of great value and had a strong fighting force and, after stringing it up, still intended to get it back for Guangdong's use. At the same time, the central government also intended to take over the ship to consolidate the strength of the sea defense. As a result of the negotiations between the two sides, the Guangdong side was extremely generous and allowed the sunk ship to belong to the central government, and all the costs of stringing it up would be borne by the central government, and the central government would send personnel to inspect and handle the stringing up matters, etc. Eaten your meat, returned your bones... these two common sayings have also become facts. But the flying eagle has been sunk for a long time, and in the future when it is strung up, can a pile of eagle bones not be corrupted? If, it turns out to be something tasteless to eat, and a chicken rib that is a pity to throw away, what will we do? Whether this soaked chicken-like eagle is useful or not, but it is a great show of humanity that the Guangdong authorities are willing to give it to the central government! Worthy for me to compose a song of praise and virtue.

Recording Old Feelings While Playing the Zhu—Jielu

—

I read Ye Chucang's "Record of Playing the Zhu on the Border", and I could not help but float a large white and said: "How great, Tieyao. You are truly a patriotic strongman in the greenwood." Watching him bind the false medicine peddler Tian Xiaoji, take the leather bags, and go with A Ran to drink Jiangnan's wedding wine. He played with cunning thieves in his palm. And the stolen Dongshan secret map was returned to Tieyao's hand. How happy it is. But, how long has it been? The map has changed color, and what more to say about being stolen? Tieyao does not do it, where is A Ran? Is the novelist's words just for self-deprecation? As far as I have heard, if it is Old North Wind, Little White Dragon, or Wang Delin, are they not the likes of Tieyao and A Ran? A guest spoke of the Yellow Slave exterminating the enemy. Yellow Slave, a native of western Liaoning, was hired by a cunning robber, Mr. Jia's family, for more than ten years. He served diligently and got Mr. Jia's pleasure. After the September 18th incident, the slave served him more carefully. Jia treated him, because they had been together for a long time, and because he was ignorant and did not understand national affairs, he made gestures and commanded him all day long without complaining. He didn't suspect him. One day, the slave stole the master's gun, suddenly got up and shot his children, a total of six. Then he fled. Mr. Jia went out on business and was spared from the disaster. It reminds me of the rebellion of Wumeng in Yunnan in the early Qing Dynasty. Many civil and military officials were killed. The rebellious Guo were rampant. They rode official horses, wore the military uniforms of generals and marshals, and held military weapons. They acted without restraint. They released the drum and music players and the servants and did not kill them, ordering them to serve their purpose. A certain righteous servant, a gunner of military rank, was dead.

Anecdotes of Famous People

— · Old Man Rice-Field Bull ·

Liang Jie'an from Guangdong, Yi Shunding from Longyang, and Zheng Xiaoxu from Marquis' Palace were all students of Zhang Zhidong, posthumously known as the Cultural Exemplar of Nanpi, from the Baobing Hall. During the late years of the Guangxu era in the former Qing Dynasty, when Zhang, as the governor of Huguang, held great power and influence, Liang and the others were his close associates. They were once known as the "Three Dragons," with Liang as the dragon's head, Yi as the dragon's belly, and Zheng as the dragon's tail. Whenever the governor had some leisure time after official duties, he would retire from public affairs and engage in casual conversation with his disciples in his quiet study, amidst the smoke of tea. The old man of Baobing Hall enjoyed using "poetry clock" with seven rounds and drinking games and mountain songs as a way to pass the long days. For example, poetry clock games like: (Lin Daiyu and a knife) "The concubine buries flowers, with tears in both eyes; the husband achieves his goal, with a head falling to the ground." (Fan Li and a flute) "The misty waters of Five Lakes are priceless in spring; the passes and mountains without villages have the sound of the moon." (Pedicure and selling court gazettes) "The effort under the feet requires a three-inch iron; the current value is only one cash." (During the Guangxu era, there were peddlers who specialized in printing clay tablets with information about newly appointed provincial officials or promotions and demotions of Beijing officials, calling them "court gazettes," each selling for one cash. After the Xuantong era, such calls were no longer heard in the market.) (Chess and mosquitoes) "Black and white crisscross, knocking on the night moon; morning and dusk faintly stir, like spring thunder." (Cao Cao and crabs) "Heroes under heaven are only me; before wine, the taste has both sharp and round." (Eliminating Cold Pictures and spring grass) "The grain man writes a small preface to the pipe; Yunbo's new poem imitates the Six Dynasties." (Tea sound and Imperial Academy Student) "Famous garden flower events have ended in prosperity; talents from the Imperial Academy are numerous and outstanding." (Qu Yuan and the painted eyebrow bird) "Casting the book into the White Water, harboring thoughts of the Chu guest; crying at dawn in the green window, calling for Zhang Lang." (Lotus leaf coin and flower list) "The young master of the Xia family finds it hard to squander; the famous courtesan of the fragrant land enters the ranks for comments." etc. Elegant and humorous, both were combined. The art world spread the word, and the price of paper in Luoyang rose. In the past thirty years, the teacher and disciples have passed away one after another. Only Jiei Yuan, the old man, doesn't realize it and follows the puppets into Shenyang. He is ashamed of his ancestor, the hermit of Banqiao, who was so much more unrestrained.

Captured and forced to be a gunner by the Jurchens. When the Jurchen army suffered a defeat, he planned to use the cannon but didn't know how. The righteous soldier pointed the muzzle upward. The Jurchens also pointed at it. Angered, he said, "It must be pointed at them." The righteous soldier deceptively said, "If so, another cannon must be made." The Jurchens allowed it. The righteous soldier broke the fuse of the cannon in a secluded place. Seeing a barrel of gunpowder nearby, he rushed to the barrel with a torch. The Jurchens hurriedly tried to stop him, but it was too late. The fire ignited, and the barrel exploded, sounding like thunder. The rocks on the mountain collapsed. The Jurchens near the fire all died, and the effects extended ten miles away. The righteous soldier also perished in the flames. Chang Lutan of the early Qing Dynasty recorded this event in the Zuihong Pavilion Collection, praising his sacrifice as saving a million lives in southern Yunnan. The death of the righteous soldier was not a death at all. Alas! A certain chauffeur during the Shanghai War, who did not hesitate to sacrifice his life and perished with the enemy's artillery shells in the Huangpu River, can also be considered to share immortality with the righteous soldier of Wumeng.

Americans and Alcohol

— Gu Dai

In the eyes of Americans, alcohol is nothing less than a second life. Before the Prohibition Act was enacted, the number of taverns was truly indescribable. Fine wines were displayed everywhere in cafes, dance halls, and even restaurants and hotels. Even in remote villages with only a few families, there would be liquor stalls. American women enjoy traveling. During their leisure time after work, they often take their partners for a drive to the suburbs. When thirsty, they would often buy wine to quench their thirst. However, the strong alcohol content often led to confusion and caused accidents. In urban areas, signs saying "Five Cents a Drink" could be seen every ten steps in residential and industrial areas. These taverns were poorly equipped, with no tables or chairs. All they had was a long counter. Those who loved to drink could pay five cents to hold a cup and drink heartily while leaning against the counter. Paying ten cents allowed them to finish two cups. Common laborers mostly got drunk here.

The day with the highest volume of alcohol sales in taverns and all entertainment venues was Saturday noon until the early morning of the following day. This was because American workers and some government employees were paid on Saturday mornings. Many used their week's earnings to buy drinks. At five cents a cup, they would drink like cattle, vomiting when drunk and continuing to drink as before, until the evening mist descended, and the lights of thousands of homes shone, or even until the night was late and their purses were empty. Only then would they dance and sing, staggering home. Wives would cry from hunger, and children would wail from cold, but they would not care. Even more were those who were too drunk to walk and would lie down in the middle of the road. It was not uncommon to see severed limbs and broken feet under the wheels of passing cars. Therefore, during the last presidential election, women with the right to vote all supported Hoover, because Hoover was the strongest advocate for Prohibition.

However, after President Hoover issued the Prohibition Act, it was implemented vigorously. It seemed that it could be completely abolished in one fell swoop, satisfying the wishes of women with husbands addicted to alcohol. But in reality, it was not so. Open sales were indeed impossible, but private brewing, private trafficking, and private sales were still everywhere. Because the prohibition was strict, the operations were extremely secretive, making it very difficult to detect and crack down. Although a few who were once immersed in alcohol were deterred by the strictness of the law and dared not try easily, generally speaking, the situation was still as prevalent as before, only changing from open to secret. Therefore, the Prohibition policy in America can be said to be a complete failure. It is rumored that in the upcoming election this winter, if Hoover is not re-elected and the opposition party comes to power, the Prohibition Act will inevitably be repealed. This is because Prohibition has not only failed to achieve any results, but the country has also reduced its tax revenue from alcohol as a result.

▲ Er Yi Zhi Tan Errata: In the "Strength and Gentleness" section, first paragraph, "people with no progress," the character "no" was mistakenly printed as "institute." In the third paragraph, "only hear the sharp knife cutting tofu," the character "one" is missing after "falling." In the "Tongue" section, "ugly ugly woman," the character "ugly" was mistakenly printed as "appearance." In the "Cai E and the Five Rivers" section, the character "Xie" in "Xie Shanshan" was mistakenly printed as "Xie" throughout.

Foreigners' Opinions on Chinese Aviation

— Listening·Zen·

The following is a translation from issue 91 of the Japanese magazine "Aviation Affairs," originally published in the British magazine "Aircraft," being a letter to the "Central, China Postal Service" magazine from a Far East correspondent stationed by our company (referring to the Aircraft magazine company itself). It is now transcribed below.

"Wake up, China! Please wake up!

No matter what the matter, whenever it is put into the hands of the Chinese to implement, it shows that you are the most incompetent country in the world." Recently, during my second visit to the Hankou airfield, I couldn't help but utter the above words in disappointment. The postal aviation service has been in operation for two years. Initially, the airfield was supposed to have considerable improvements, but instead, not only has this not happened, but the Chinese government is constantly undermining itself. How can this be? The postal airplanes still take off and land in a corner of the airfield that is both filthy and chaotic. The hangars (referring to the storage houses for airplanes) are still crammed with military airplanes in a mess. What's worse, outside the hangars, there are many broken, damaged, and dilapidated airplanes piled up like "a mountain," with no one bothering to take care of them. This situation would startle even the most heartless traveler, leaving them speechless.

In a barracks as filthy as a pigsty, a squad of soldiers in beggar-like clothing squats there, doing nothing all day.

On a road half-submerged in puddles, there are two sentry tents lying in disarray, which is especially infuriating. What's more, sentries are actually posted there, but without any rules or regulations. If travelers want to pass through this area to reach the airplane parking area, they can't pass through casually. If you try to explain this to them, they won't understand at all, which is very frustrating. It seems that the officers have never taught the sentries what their duties are. So what is the purpose of setting up these sentries? It's really inexplicable.

Besides this vast open space, there are no toilets provided for the military or travelers. As a result, after a long time, urine and feces can be found everywhere.

For weighing postal letters or luggage, there is indeed a scale-like object placed there for weighing purposes, but its appearance makes one suspect that it is "difficult to be accurate." Because of the management methods described above, it is no wonder that the airfield has repeatedly become like a muddy sea. Now, it has simply become a lake surface. I personally saw an airplane, during takeoff, carrying mud and water as high as fifteen feet, covering the passengers, seats, and luggage with rotten mud, turning them all into mud people. During takeoff, they always try to leave the ground four or five times. Each time they take off, they drag mud and water. This time, it seems to be able to take off, but it stops again and has to start over again. Do you think the passengers can bear it?

Wake up, China! If you really want to revitalize the aviation industry, then this cannot continue. It is hoped that you will build a proper airfield and use the common sense that can maintain this industry. Try to open your eyes and see how the airplanes and passengers are being messed with in that area! See if your useless soldiers are hindering your industry! Prove whether my words are unfair. As for the soldiers, I will now say a little opinion in passing, although it is not within the scope of this topic, rather than wasting the country's useful money to raise these soldiers who stand on one leg like old chickens and suffer from "rheumatism" (a disease that can hinder the "operation of aircraft," that is, paralysis, the original text is very descriptive of their deformity), it is better to use it for the drainage project in the flooded barracks. Canadians are good at speaking frankly, please forgive me!

According to this article, which is a Japanese magazine translating a British magazine, the description is extremely sarcastic. Reading it makes one feel ashamed and greatly reduces one's desire to study aviation. In order to make the public universally understand what foreigners think of our aviation, I have spared no effort in my busy work to translate this from the Japanese magazine to provide everyone with a cold sweat. However, the Japanese translator originally noted that "the authenticity of the facts is unclear, and it may not be so severe." In my humble opinion, perhaps the correspondent visited after the great flood in Hankou, so it is no wonder that there is such a phenomenon. Listening Zen again.

Gold Exchange Rate Falls, Gold Price Rises

▲ Market Fluctuations Occurred Yesterday's gold exchange rate fell and then rose again, but without any special changes. There was a slight upward trend, with intermittent fluctuations totaling about four taels in price difference. Dealers' sentiment remained uncertain, with frequent entries and exits. Ultimately, the price rose by more than four taels, reaching a high. Although the silver market rose, the forward silver price fell instead, leading to a higher opening. As the foreign exchange market appeared stable, with hidden strength, gold dealers sold British gold slightly, while American dollars continued to be shorted to counter the price. The market had more buyers, pushing prices down, with occasional fluctuations of more than two taels. Later, due to short covering, prices rebounded. In the afternoon, as it was Wednesday, there were frequent holidays. The September-October swap that had not been completed was done by Hengxing, posting a difference of five qian, while other firms still had more than four thousand taels unswapped. It is said that the new trading volume for the October term was about twenty-one thousand taels. The details of the morning market are recorded below.

▲ Rebound of Four Taels and Four Qian The September term opened, rising four taels and six qian, to 713 taels and eight qian. Large orders for the near term remained as before, with the far term increasing by one-eighth. Silver prices also rose by one-quarter, but this had no effect. Private cables did not change. The exchange rate of British pounds fell while the American dollar rose, so the market sentiment was upward. Then, it decreased by three qian, with buyers from all sides exceeding usual. Hengyu, Fuyu, Yuhe, Dadecheng, Zhifengyong, and others all competed to buy. Also, the exchange market seemed better, with China Bank absorbing British gold for December at 195625, and doing American dollars for September at thirty-one yuan. Therefore, the gold price increased by more than one tael in a frenzy, to fifteen taels and two qian. Shortly after, Yuanxing, Yongyifeng, Yongyong, Yuanheng, Yuanmao, Yongyi, and others all divested. And because the American dollar eased, Mitsui came out with October at 125, and Anda and American Express did December at half a yuan, so it fell again by more than three taels, with only a small profit of one tael, reaching eleven taels and eight qian at 9:20 AM. Suddenly, it increased by two taels, to thirteen taels and seven or eight qian, because Qianchang, Xiangfutai, Hengyuantai, Yuhe, and others entered the market. The opening price of British gold did not change, and the American dollar hung large at 125, but it had no impact. The domestic market was still flat, slightly lower by four or five qian. In an instant, it soared again, with Hengchang, Yongyifeng, Yongyong, Bingxing, Hengxing entering the market to buy, so it became fifteen taels and one qian. Subsequently, there were fluctuations of more than two taels, but sellers were active. After 10 AM, HSBC came out with British gold for September at 375, Zhengjin came out with November at 5625, and Hengchang, Yongheng, Yuzhifengyong, Zhaofengchang, Hengxingyuan, and others all sold vigorously, while Hengxing bought, as the price had fallen to around thirteen taels. After 10:30 AM, it became more and more tired, with Huabi coming out with thirty-one yuan for this month, 375 for November, and Fuyu, Yongfeng, Hongkangyong, Xiexingyong, and others following suit to sell, continuing to decline by two or three taels. At 11 AM, it suddenly became ten taels and five qian, but Daxingyong, Hengyu, Zhifengyong dragged it in, and Huabi and Makari absorbed British gold for October at 19 and a half, plus more than one tael, totaling twelve taels and three qian. At that time, there was another small profit of one qian. After 11:30 AM, it rebounded again, as Makari absorbed British gold for November at 5625. The buying momentum on the table suddenly increased, with Yuankangxiang, Daxingyong, Yuanyong, Dayongyuhe, and others making efforts to enter. Also, some small short sellers did not want to carry over to the next day, so they followed to buy, turning from weakness to strength in an instant, jumping more than three taels, with the profit being only a few qian, reaching fourteen taels and six qian at 11:50 AM. However, many small long-term holders took this opportunity to sell, and Zhifengyong, Hengyu, Yifengyong also sold slightly, causing the price to fall again. At the noon closing, it was thirteen taels and six qian, continuing to trade within thirteen taels, a rebound of four taels and four qian compared to the previous day (according to the listed price). According to the confusing market conditions, it is difficult to grasp the situation. In short, people's hearts are not settled, and they are losing their measures. The maximum price for half a day was fifteen taels and two qian, the minimum price was ten taels and a half, with a difference of four taels and seven qian. The net taels totaled nine taels.

▲ Discount Reduced by Seven Taels The discount was changed to 787 taels, because the American dollar was hung high at 125, estimating the reduction to be 73 to 77 taels. The noon closing was 74 to 75 taels, a reduction of seven taels compared to the previous day. The amounts recorded for each month were all 14 taels, and the water supplement was 13 taels.

▲ Complex Trading Among Various Firms Trading on the table was still active, but the situation was complex. According to statistics, Zhifengyong, Yifengyong, Hengxing, Bingxing, Yuankangxiang, Yuhe, Yuantai, Kaitai, Hengchangyong, Futaiheng all entered. Yuanxingyong, Yuanheng, Xiexingyong, Taifengcheng, Yongfeng, Hengxingyuan all exited. Yuanmaoyong, Yuandayong, Hengyu, Shunli, Fuyu, Wanxing, Zhaofengchang, Daxingyong, Hongkangyong, etc., had quite a lot of back-and-forth trading. The Ningbo firms collectively entered more than four hundred taels and sold more than three hundred taels. The Guangdong firms, such as Hengxing, bought five or six hundred taels, but the number of sellers was less.

New York Stock Market Continues to Rise

(Report from the American Eastern Bank Corporation)

▲ Opening Momentum Unmatched ▲ Struck by Plunging Wheat Prices

On Tuesday, the New York stock market continued the upward trend from Monday. The opening saw immediate strength, and trading was extremely active. Within the first hour, 800,000 shares changed hands, a rare occurrence. Based on the prevailing conditions, the market was expected to develop even further. However, soon after, wheat prices were reported to have plummeted drastically. Although this event caused some concern, the overall sentiment remained strong. Therefore, the market was not greatly affected. Taking U.S. Steel shares as an example, the previous week's closing price was $40.125. On Tuesday's opening, it immediately jumped to $45, closing at $43.125. Railroad stocks were relatively stable, with Union Pacific Railroad, a representative stock, rising by $4.50 from the previous day. Utility stocks performed best with American Telephone & Telegraph, which also rose by $4.50 from the previous day. Judging from the current stock market situation, it appears that wheat prices will be the determining factor. If wheat prices continue to fall, the stock market will be severely affected. Conversely, if wheat prices can quickly rebound, the stock market will continue to rise. Attached below are the Dow Jones indices for Tuesday:

Grains

He Xia Rice Market Firm

▲Yesterday, arrivals from all sources in Shanghai South were less than 10 ships, and stocks at the docks have become scarce again. Arrivals of Changshu and Wuxi japonica rice were particularly abundant. Local retailers favored early indica rice the most, with bulk prices remaining stable. Native banks showed little interest, and prices decreased by 5 fen. New japonica rice was sold as soon as it arrived, and there was no supply of Glutinous rice available. Foreign glutinous rice was affected by foreign rice prices, with prices lower by several cents.

The market is becoming increasingly flat and listless, with limited fluctuations. Top-quality Changshu and Wuxi rice is slightly softer. Arrivals of indica rice are sparse, with sluggish sales. Market prices have hardened slightly by several cents. New japonica rice sales are still good, and prices remain firm. Native banks showed slight interest in foreign glutinous rice, with no price increases or decreases. Arrivals from Wuxi, Jiangyin, Yixing, Songjiang, Fengjing, Jiashan, Tongli, and other locations totaled approximately 2,000 piculs from 15-16 He Xia cargo boats.

Initial Weakness Followed by Stability in the Flour Market

▲ The Flour Exchange Restores Full-Day Trading Today.

Yesterday, the flour market showed initial weakness followed by stability in all months after the morning opening. Foreign wheat prices retreated by a small margin of 2-3 cents, and non-industry sentiment was quite weak. However, although market sentiment was poor, northern buyers continued to purchase actively. Therefore, prices gradually rebounded in subsequent trading sessions. As for the mills, only a few offered flour, as it was difficult to sell. Without significant fluctuations in foreign wheat prices and with continued active buying, there is no expectation of further declines. As a result, August and September contracts were up 2.5 li from the previous day, October, November, and December contracts were up 5 li, and January contracts were up 2.5 li. Starting from the 18th, the flour exchange will restore full-day trading, with trading hours from 10:00 AM to 2:30 PM.

This Month's Wheat Sales Are Particularly Strong

Yesterday's wheat market saw foreign wheat prices down by a small margin of 2-3 cents in all months after the morning opening. Non-industry buying was also not active, and a soft trend was evident in the consolidation. However, at the afternoon opening, the current month's market suddenly showed weakness as large longs were eager to sell. It was rumored that the deliverable quantity for the current month was between 3-5 truckloads, but the collection of goods had not yet been centralized, resulting in strong selling pressure and an unstable market. Distant months also showed slight declines. As a result, August fell by 7 fen, September fell by 4 fen, October fell by 3 fen, November fell by 2 fen, and December fell by 1 fen. The spot wheat market was slightly more active, with Wusong wheat opening at 3 taels, 3 mace, and 8 fen, Guzhen wheat at 3 taels, 8 mace, and 5 fen, Jiangbei wheat at 3 taels, 4 mace, and 5 fen, Zhenjiang wheat at 3 taels, 3 mace, and 7 fen, Penglai wheat at 3 taels, 3 mace, and 4 fen, and Chongming wheat at 3 taels, 3 mace, and 5 fen, totaling over 1,300 bags.

Foreign Rice Remains Stable

The foreign rice market was not active yesterday. However, sellers were holding firm due to high costs, and the amount of rice in circulation was less than one-third of the total inventory. Although the total inventory in the city was over 1.3 million bags, some were stored in Japanese merchant warehouses, some had not been converted into warehouse receipts, and some were pledged and not moving. Therefore, sentiment turned stable, and the market did not show significant weakness. The total quantity offered in the market yesterday was less than 2,000 bags, with Saigon rice and glutinous rice each accounting for half. Saigon medium-grade rice No. 1 was purchased by native banks from Wuxi at a price of 9 yuan and 8 jiao. Glutinous rice was priced at 9 yuan and 4 jiao to 9 yuan, 3 jiao, and 2 fen. Old glutinous rice was priced at 9 yuan and 1 jiao to 9 yuan and 5 fen, all purchased by local village households.

Silk and Tea

European and American Silk Sales Sluggish

Overseas raw silk markets, following the sharp rise of Japanese silk, have experienced a subsequent sharp decline. Telegrams from Shanghai to European and American silk companies have not seen any improvement. European and American companies are taking a wait-and-see approach, and Chinese silk merchants are also maintaining a firm stance, resulting in a sluggish market. Yesterday, only Qianli and Yihe purchased 20 bales of Sichuan Yellow silk from the Tieji 13-15 size at a price of 510 taels, and Dachang purchased 5 bales of Shandong Yellow silk from the medium size 13-15 size at a price of 520 taels.

Shandong Yellow Silk Stocks Gradually Depleting

▲ Shanghai Stocks Below 3,000 Bales

With no improvement in European and American sales of Shandong Yellow silk, and with silk prices plummeting, Shandong silk merchants are selling at a loss, resulting in thin Shanghai stocks. With improved American sales of White factory silk, American companies are also starting to purchase Shandong Yellow silk, leading to transactions in recent days. Shanghai warehouse stocks are gradually depleting. A survey of Shandong factory silk in various silk warehouses shows that there are only over 2,900 bales.

Needle and Xiu Mei Teas Sell Well, Prices Rise

Yesterday, both "Lu Zhuang" and local "Tu Zhuang" Needle and Xiu Mei green teas saw strong interest from British and French companies. However, stocks in the market have been depleted. Chinese merchants are taking an increasingly firm stance, and Needle Mei prices have risen again by four or five taels. Jinlong, Yihe, and other firms all have demand. The market trend is stable and unchanged. However, there are no major transactions for Zhen Mei and Gong Xi teas. British firms have sent many telegrams in recent days, and sentiment remains firm.

Sugar Market

Coarse Granulated White Sugar Market Slightly Firm

▲ Taikoo Sugar's Quota Market Turns Softer

Yesterday, trading volume in the Sugar Guild market was not high. The transaction price for Dutch Sugar No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar was 14 taels, 5 mace, and 5 fen. Goods at this warehouse were 14 taels and 6 mace. The price for goods where the buyer pays the outstanding taxes was 14 taels and 2 mace and 5 fen. Shipments were scarce, and the market was firm. No. 16 medium granulated white sugar was 13 taels and 7 mace and 5 fen, No. 14 raw granulated red sugar was 12 taels and 6 mace and 5 fen, and Dutch red sugar No. 8/9 was 10 taels, 0 mace, 6 and 7 fen. Transactions were sporadic. Since the factory price of Taikoo Sugar was raised, the price has increased by 1 mace. However, with the decline in gold prices, Quota costs are very high. As a result, shipments from the trading houses have increased, and the Quota market has gradually declined. B Mark was 16 taels, 2 mace, and 5 fen to 2 mace, C.W. Mark was 15 taels, 7 mace, and 5 fen to 7 mace, and H.X. Mark was 15 taels, 2 mace to 1 mace and 5 fen. Although trading is still active, sellers feel looser, and the trend is flat and weak. There seems to be little hope for the time being.

Textiles

New Autumn Woolen Fabric Demand Activated

Bījī, Huate Ni, floral fabric, Qiaokeding, and straight raincoats, which are typically sold in early autumn, are all selling well. Local customers are continuing to inquire and trade. Melton, felt, felt bottoms, various woolen fabrics, and heavy overcoat fabrics, which are typically sold in winter, are also appearing on the market. This is due to the cooler weather. The future of woolen fabrics is expected to improve day by day.

Oil Market

Asphalt Autumn Sales Activated

Asphalt summer sales have ended. It is now mid-July, and tanners are preparing to start work. However, with the first gusts of autumn wind and the heat not yet subsided, preparations have been delayed. However, traders must prepare inventory to meet the demand from tanners. Shanghai relies on Hankou for supply, and Zhejiang oil prices are high, so most purchases are made in Hankou. However, Hankou inventories have been scarce for a long time, so any transaction leads to a price increase. According to recent details from Hankou, various locations are preparing for autumn tanning, and sales are gradually becoming active. The market has also shown a sudden improvement. Macheng oil is selling for 18 taels, and Chongjing is selling for 17 taels, 2 or 3 mace, which is more than 1 tael higher than before. Autumn sales have just begun, inventories are depleted everywhere, and the intensity of the market is just beginning to emerge.

Coal

White Briquette Customer Sales Gradually Increasing

Yesterday, sales of white coal were quite good. A coal merchant from Henan purchased 170 tons of Coal briquettes from Ningbo, priced at 19 taels. A merchant from Hangzhou purchased 80 tons, priced at 5 fen less. Another 60 tons of Jidu Coal briquettes were priced at 17 taels and 5 mace. A merchant from Jiaxing purchased 100 tons of Mark Coal briquettes, priced at 18 taels, and 114 tons of Liujiang Coal briquettes, priced at 13 taels and 7 mace and 5 fen.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Examination Hall

— Fo

Mentioning examination halls makes me sad again. The other day, I calculated the cost of education for children. It costs 4,000 silver dollars for one student to graduate from a domestic university. Now, talking about examination halls means that even with money, there are no good schools to study in. It's truly pitiful.

The schools in the interior are often poorly run with lower standards. This is an undeniable fact. Shanghai schools are more complete, so residents of Shanghai naturally send their children to study in Shanghai schools. Even those living in the interior send their children to Shanghai in batches to study. But once in Shanghai, which school to try to get into? That's where the difficulty arises. Comparing the schools with better reputations and more complete content, there are actually very few in Shanghai. Even the few more famous schools are very difficult to get into. The number of openings is limited, while the number of applicants is extremely crowded. Assuming there are only 100 openings, there are often more than 1,000 applicants. Getting into such a school is more difficult than passing the imperial examination to become a scholar.

So, some people who know the principals ask them for help, and some who know the teachers ask them to speak up. If they don't know anyone directly, they ask someone to introduce them. After much effort and careful planning, if they succeed, it's considered a stroke of luck, and they shout congratulations. If they are rejected because the quota is full, would they keep their children at home and not let them study? They reluctantly consider the next best option and choose a school with a slightly lower reputation to apply to. But even these schools are not easy to get into, so they ask others for help in the same way. If they still don't succeed, they have no choice but to send their children to a general "wild chicken" type school.

Fortunately, there are many such "wild chicken" schools, like cigarette paper shops on the street. You can say that every street has them. Their principle is like Han Xin leading troops: the more, the better. Their only good point is that they only recognize money, not people. As long as you pay the tuition on time, you can study or not, it doesn't matter to them. They have several advantages, which I can briefly mention.

One: They have more holidays (because every extra day of holiday means one less day of food costs).

Two: They hire incompetent teachers (the principal is thrifty, calculating teachers' salaries by the month. If it's less than a month, they calculate by the hour, so good teachers don't want to go there).

Three: The school curriculum is sloppy (the subjects required by the ministry's regulations naturally cannot be omitted. The regulations may be grand, but the lessons can be shallow. For example, a history and geography teacher may also teach English, or an English teacher may also teach other subjects, accommodating as needed).

Four: The school has no order (these "wild chicken" schools are naturally most afraid of disturbances or students saying bad things about them, so they don't dare to be too strict with the students).

Their advantages are too numerous to list. I've only mentioned four. However, graduating from such a school presents another difficulty. After graduating from primary school, they can't get into good middle schools. After graduating from middle school, they can't get into good universities. So, graduates from "wild chicken" primary schools can only go to "wild chicken" middle schools, and graduates from "wild chicken" middle schools can only go to "wild chicken" universities. These students are always stuck in these "wild chicken" schools as apprentices. In the end, they become "wild chicken" university graduates, which is such a pitiful thing.

Literature and Art

French Park

— Dashe

Dense summer trees shade the sky,

Fragrant dew opens paired lotus.

The stars should laugh at their yearly crossing,

Do not compare loved ones to deities.

After the chaos, flowers and birds leave cries of tears,

The calamity's writing consigns sand worms to oblivion.

Do not listen to the songs of Wu, your heart will easily break,

Suddenly meet a traveler from Chu, and their eyes will shine green.

The wind blows tree leaves, stirring the sound of commerce,

Tides surge, fish and dragons give the night air a fishy stench.

I lie on the vast river, autumn is about to arrive,

Cultivating frosted temples, both temples like stars.

Science

The Latest Air Conditioning System

— Baitao

Recently, major movie theaters and large hotels are promoting themselves with the latest air conditioning systems. What exactly is this new type of air conditioning system? I suppose that is what you, the readers, would like to know.

The electric cooling device in the new air conditioning system is really a new type of cooling method for modern households. But the scientific principle it applies is extremely simple. Everyone knows that under normal circumstances, water needs to be heated to 212 degrees Fahrenheit to boil. But in a vacuum or at high altitudes, it will boil at a very low temperature. In a vacuum chamber, water boils without fire. Once water boils, it evaporates quickly. That is to say, the water turns into an invisible gas! At this time, it absorbs a large amount of heat. When you wash your body with water, you feel very refreshed after it is wet. This is because when the water on your body evaporates into gas, it takes away a lot of heat from your body, so you feel cool. The electric cooling device is made using this principle.

The cooler contains a very high vacuum chamber, which is created by pumping all the air out of the chamber with a pump. This vacuum chamber allows the liquid to evaporate at a low temperature, and it evaporates into water vapor at a very high speed, absorbing a large amount of heat from the air. Then, the gas is passed through a tube into a condenser, which includes a set of cooling devices (pools, honeycomb radiators, electric fans, etc.) that condense the water vapor into water. The water flows from another tube back into the evaporator, and the cycle continues.

The pump and fan are all powered by a generator, so it is called an electric cooling device.

Recently, there is a newer type of air conditioning system that uses gas flames! This flame is not a fire flame, but a freezing cold air! This freezing cold air can evaporate the coolant, resulting in the recovery of heat and the spraying of cold water, which still changes from gas to liquid. This new type of air conditioning system does not require an electric motor.

There are many of these new type cooling systems in Shanghai lately, When a person feels the scorching heat, being in it, can forget a lot of the heat.

Society Improvement Discussion Group

Proposal to Establish a Crèche

— Wu

Since the commencement of discussions at this conference, some issues, perhaps quite crucial, have been addressed and resolved as thoroughly as possible within the realm of "improvement." I, in my inadequacy, have rarely participated, merely observing the bustling activity during my daily newspaper reading. Consequently, I acknowledge my failure to fulfill the duty incumbent upon every member. However, rather than offering insincere opinions, I have chosen to remain silent, believing this to be more beneficial for my personal cultivation. But now, I am breaking my silence, prepared to present a more practical issue here.

Originally, many issues can only be resolved in a different kind of society, that is, a society where its economic and political machinery has undergone fundamental changes. Many problems that cannot be solved in the real society will inevitably be completely solved because of the change in their economic foundation. However, there are also a few problems that can be considerably improved even in the real society. Although this limited improvement is far from sufficient, it can ultimately lay a cornerstone for the future grand "transformation." In that case, the following proposal may have some significance.

Isn't it true that many gentlemen who pay attention to social ills constantly "lament" the inequality between men and women? Don't many well-educated ladies often feel regretful about being constantly excluded from the political sphere? Don't many hardworking women constantly suffer from male oppression because they cannot engage in production? Of course, these are all inevitable results of China's unique deformed social and political state. However, the bondage of children to their mothers is also the greatest obstacle to women's liberation.

Four thousand years of history have bestowed upon women a supreme belief: a multitude of children is the greatest blessing for mothers. However, this has also predetermined the lifelong destiny of mothers, that is, to become beasts of burden for their children from then on, entrusting everything to the growth and prosperity of their children. In terms of physiology, all women will inevitably have children, and once they have children, they must raise them to adulthood. Moreover, the task of raising children seems to be the sole responsibility of women. Therefore, this is simply a non-issue. However, I believe that if crèches were established, the relationship between mothers and children could be reduced in many ways. I will elaborate on this from various perspectives as follows:

(1) With the organization of crèches, women can reduce the burden of the family and engage in the liberation movement to seek political and economic equality.

(2) Women will not be excluded from the political sphere or lag behind the political level due to the bondage of children.

(3) Laboring women can directly participate in production to seek economic independence and reduce the burden on their husbands.

(4) The development of this kind of organization can enable a portion of women to obtain suitable occupations (serving in crèches).

(5) Children can have healthy bodies through scientific parenting methods.

(6) Children can become accustomed to group life and receive good children's education. Naturally, only with children who are physically healthy and well-educated can the nation have a future for development.

The above explains the significance of establishing crèches. As for how to establish and equip them, it is beyond the scope of one person's opinion. Group efforts are essential for success. In this regard, I sincerely hope that enlightened members will not hesitate to offer guidance, so that it can be realized perfectly.

Finally, there is an additional statement: a certain lady is already actively working to realize this plan. However, due to the lack of funds and talent, it may not be completed for a while. Therefore, in addition to attempting to spark heated discussions here, I am also appealing to society on behalf of the lady, urging fellow advocates to provide powerful assistance.

Family Questions

A Family Next Door to a "Study Residence"

— Wei

Next door to the ancestral home of the Chen family mansion, there was a "study residence" - home to the most famous courtesan in Shanghai. Every night, deep into the night, the lights were bright, the wine was green, people were talking, and the flowers were fragrant, which was the human hell where grease, powder, and bones were eroded and vanished! However, next door was the residence of a certain XX school principal, who was very humble and had the demeanor of a gentleman of integrity. He had only one daughter named Zhenshu, a little girl who did not know the ways of the world, lively by nature, and of good character and appearance. Because the neighbor was a "study residence", Mr. Chen often told her ancient stories of female loyalty, filial piety, chastity, and righteousness in detail, so that she would never forget these good teachings. However, those who are near ink get stained black. The laughter and happy sounds all night long, and the strange and bizarre costumes of the courtesans, stained a spot of pure white on Zhenshu's heart.

Five or six years later, Mr. Chen saw that his daughter's every move had changed. What she had seen and heard in the brothel and "study residence" had wiped out Mr. Chen's more than ten years of family education. He often saw her deliberately imitating the courtesans' dressing style when she came back from school, and she had learned the ugly attitude of flirting and scolding. She even sang the little tunes of "Four Seasons of Yearning" and "Playing Dominoes." Her father was so angry and resentful that he died depressed!

From then on, Zhenshu became more and more unrestrained and dissolute. Someone returning from Suzhou said! Outside the Chumen Gate, on the A'dai Bridge, there is indeed a brightly colored Chen Haohao who stands alone! She is set to be the most beautiful courtesan at the Jinchang Pavilion!

She finally fell! Her fall was due to the word "near" in "those who are near vermilion get stained red, and those who are near ink get stained black"!

Joke

Country Folk Don't Understand Western Languages

— Chao Chen

A child from the countryside, newly returned home from school for summer vacation, was reciting English spelling: "P. E. P." "P. W. P." He repeated these two phrases more than a hundred times. A pedantic scholar happened to pass by outside the door and sighed upon hearing this, "This child can be said to understand the principles of books. He says, 'worn leather garment,' 'discard when worn.' This is the meaning of what Confucius said in the Analects: 'Wearing a light fur coat, discard it without regret.'" Worn leather garment means the fur coat is already broken. Discard when worn means discard it when it is broken and there is no need to resent it. A hooligan, A Da, passed by the door a little later and became furious when he heard this, "This child is hateful. He takes me as a bully and wants to avoid me, repeatedly saying 'avoid a bit,' 'avoid a bully.' His words are impolite. I must argue with him." A few moments later, a crooked-mouthed A Er passed by and sneered, "This child dares to mock my crooked mouth. Knowing that my lower jaw is crooked, he wants to compare with me, saying, 'compare a bit,' 'compare the lower jaw.' How impish!" After a while, a hoarse-throated A San passed by and was indignant, "This is too much to deceive, laughing at my throat being too low, a slight change and it becomes mute, saying 'change a bit,' 'change mute.' What grudge does he have against me that he curses me to be mute?" Thereupon, the hooligan A Da, crooked-mouthed A Er, and hoarse-throated A San entered the door together, wanting to pummel the child. Fortunately, the pedantic scholar hurried inside to cite book verses to explain the misunderstanding, and the child was spared from danger.

▲Liu Longbao versus Shu Rongdu for Debt (Main Text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of one thousand eight hundred silver dollars. The first item of this judgment shall be subject to provisional execution. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲Li Yitang versus Shen Xianchen for Execution Objection (Main Text): The disputed house and foundation located at No. 133, Dongbaoxing Road, Shanghai, shall be exempt from provisional execution. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲Feng Jiabang versus Li Wen for Land Rental Appeal (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The second instance litigation costs are borne by the appellant.

▲Peng Xueying versus Cai Yimin for Dissolution of Marriage (Main Text): The plaintiff's claim is dismissed. The litigation costs are borne by the plaintiff. Chen Guansheng versus Zhang Rongsheng et al. for Rent and Eviction (Main Text): Defendant Zhang Rongsheng shall pay the plaintiff rent of one hundred and fifty silver dollars. Defendant Chen Linsheng shall pay the plaintiff rent of one hundred and six silver dollars. Defendant Ou Rongqing shall pay the plaintiff rent of one hundred and twenty silver dollars. Defendant Li Yaoting shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and forty-nine silver dollars. Huang Liansheng shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and forty-nine silver dollars. Fu Hongde shall pay the plaintiff rent of one hundred and twenty-one silver dollars. Bao Shikui shall pay the plaintiff rent of one hundred and six silver dollars. Chen Jinchun shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and forty-nine silver dollars. Shen Zigao shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and forty silver dollars. Zhou A'gen shall pay the plaintiff rent of two hundred and sixty-six silver dollars. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The litigation costs are borne by the defendants Li Yaoting, Huang Liansheng, Chen Jinchun, Shen Zigao, and Zhou A'gen equally for sixty percent, and Zhang Rongsheng, Xu Linsheng, Ouyang Rongchun, Fu Hongde, and Bao Shikui equally for forty percent. Zheng Pin Yang versus Hu Jingdun for House Rental (Main Text): Defendant Hu Jingdun shall repay the plaintiff rent of seventy-two silver dollars. Defendants Zhang Xiulian and Tu Zhonggui shall each repay the plaintiff rent of fifty-four silver dollars and each shall vacate the house. The litigation costs are borne equally by the defendants. Gu Jingqing versus Chen Shuqing et al. for Rent Arrears (Main Text): The defendants shall pay the plaintiff rent arrears of forty silver dollars. If they are unable to pay, Guangfeng Firm shall be responsible for payment on their behalf. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant Chen Shuping.

▲Ding Zhu's versus Wang Defa for House Rental (Main Text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of ninety-eight silver dollars and litigation costs of thirty-six silver dollars and shall vacate the house. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant. The first item of this judgment regarding vacation shall be subject to provisional execution.

▲Gu Zimei versus Zhou Rongting et al. for Rent Arrears (Main Text): Defendant Zhou Rongting shall pay the plaintiff one hundred and sixty-eight silver dollars. Zhang Dengyun shall pay the plaintiff fifty silver dollars. Each shall vacate the houses located at Nos. 11-12, Yongxingfang. The litigation costs are borne by the defendants proportionally.

▲Zhu Liangfu versus Yang Mingzhi for Divorce (Main Text): The marriage between the plaintiff and the defendant is approved for divorce. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant.

▲Service by Public Notice: Liang Kun versus Xu Yaowu for Rent Arrears Case: This court has scheduled a public hearing for 9:00 AM on September 9th. The defendant is instructed to appear in court on time for argument and shall not delay on their own accord. This is a special public notice to the defendant Xu Yaowu for their information. (The above are for August 17th)

Shanghai Local Court

▲Criminal Judgments Wang Yungeng and others case of obstructing freedom (Verdict): This prosecution is not accepted. ▲Zhang Miaogen case of obstructing freedom and assault (Verdict): Zhang Miaogen is fined fifty yuan for illegal detention. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory execution, one yuan will be converted to one day of imprisonment, and one hemp rope will be confiscated. ▲Lu Xiang case of fraud (Verdict): Lu Xiang, with the intention of illegal possession, is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for habitual fraud, with deprivation of public rights for five years. The number of days in custody will be converted to imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. ▲Zhang Shenshi case of opium (Verdict): Zhang Shenshi is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for possessing opium with the intention of selling it, and is also fined fifty yuan. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory execution, one yuan will be converted to one day of imprisonment. The number of days in custody will be converted to imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. Forty-five taels of opium are confiscated. ▲Chen Bingquan case of obstructing freedom and fraud (Verdict): Chen Bingquan is sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for enticing women with the intention of profit. He is also sentenced to two months of imprisonment for attempting to induce others to hand over their possessions through fraudulent means. The combined sentence is one year and seven months. The number of days in custody will be converted to imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. ▲Xu Xiaobin case of obstructing freedom and fraud (Verdict): This prosecution is not accepted. ▲Zhuang Zhiyan case of assault (Verdict): This prosecution is not accepted. Ruling: Appeal against Xu Afu case of causing death by negligence (Verdict): Appeal dismissed. Ye Rensheng case of theft (Verdict): Ye Rensheng is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for continuous theft at the train station. The number of days in custody will be converted to imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. ▲Li Tiansheng sues Jin Awu et al. for assault (Verdict): This private prosecution is dismissed. ▲Cao Shanqi et al. case of theft (Verdict): Cao Shanqi and Ji Decheng are each sentenced to twenty days of detention for theft. The number of days in custody will be converted to detention at a rate of two days for one day. ▲Shao Yangui et al. case of opium (Verdict): Shao Tinggui and Cao Jinshi are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment for smoking opium, and are also fined thirty yuan. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory execution, one yuan will be converted to one day of imprisonment. The number of days in custody will be converted to imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day, or one day for one yuan of fine. One opium pipe, one lamp, and ten red pills are confiscated.

▲Criminal Instructions Xu Huasheng requested a warrant for Chen Ziyi's embezzlement. The petition states that the defendant's whereabouts are unknown. It is instructed that if the defendant is found, the local police should be notified to arrest and escort him to the court. A note should be added to the warrant stating that, based on the request, letters will be sent to all relevant authorities for unified assistance in apprehending and bringing the defendant to justice. This is the instruction.

▲Civil Judgments Shu Zhixing vs. Ma Zhangfu et al. case of debt (Verdict): The defendant Ma Zhangfu shall repay the plaintiff 150 yuan in principal and 30 yuan in interest. If he is unable to repay, the defendant Xu Guiqing shall be responsible for repayment. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant Ma Zhangfu. Zhou Lianzhen vs. Wang Huanzhi case of debt appeal (Verdict): Appeal dismissed. The appeal costs shall be borne by the appellant. ▲Jiang Cezi vs. Ying Jinrong case of deposit (Verdict): The plaintiff's claim is dismissed. This case should be transferred to Lanxi County Court for adjudication. ▲Zhang Mei vs. Zhang Xucui case of cohabitation (Verdict): The defendant shall cohabit with the plaintiff. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲Zhou Zhushi vs. Zhou Chengshu case of separation (Verdict): The plaintiff's claim is dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff. ▲Hong Shaoxian vs. Zhuo Quansheng case of bill of exchange (Verdict): The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 200 yuan for the bill of exchange, plus interest calculated at an annual rate of six percent from April 22nd of the 20th year of the Republic of China until the date of execution. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲Yang Zhoushi vs. Yang Zengfu case of divorce and alimony (Verdict): The plaintiff's claim is dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff. ▲Yu Xiaomei vs. Wu Yongxing case of divorce and cohabitation (Verdict): The plaintiff's claim is dismissed. The plaintiff shall cohabit with the defendant. The litigation costs for both the original and counterclaim shall be borne by the plaintiff.

▲Civil Instructions Zhu Xiquan petitioned for the preservation of ancestral graves due to his son selling family land. The petition states that if there are private rights disputes, a formal lawsuit should be filed for adjudication. The request for preservation should not be discussed. This is the instruction. ▲Gu Zhangshi and Gu Jinye agreed to a divorce and requested it to be filed. The petition states that since they have agreed to a divorce, the request should be approved. This is the instruction. (Above are from August 16th)

This is the instruction. ▲Wang Lianqing petitioned for strict execution. The petition states that the matter should be strictly pursued. This is the instruction. ▲Lu Xuekui petitioned for strict execution. The petition states that the matter should be strictly pursued after arrest. This is the instruction. ▲Yang Jiakun petitioned for appointment. The petition states that the request is approved. This is the instruction. ▲Mai Sesheng petitioned for execution. The petition states that the case is under appeal and the request should be temporarily deferred. This is the instruction. ▲Huang Gaoshi petitioned for appointment. The petition states that the request is approved. This is the instruction. ▲Gu Zizhen petitioned for an extension of the deadline for arrest. The petition states that the request is approved. This is the instruction. ▲Gu Jingqing petitioned for execution. The petition states that the petitioner should come to the court for questioning at 10:00 AM on the 17th of this month. This is the instruction. (Above are from August 13th)
